# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# GCC RTL Intermediate Representation Pass Chain

## Your Task

Trace how GCC's RTL (Register Transfer Language) passes are organized and executed in gcc. Find C++ source files implementing: the RTL pass class, the pass_expand (gimple to RTL), a representative RTL optimization pass, and the final code generation pass.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d, sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've successfully traced and documented the GCC RTL pass chain. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary of GCC RTL Pass Chain

I've identified the key components of GCC's RTL intermediate representation and pass architecture:

### **RTL Pass Class Hierarchy** (`gcc/tree-pass.h`)
- **`opt_pass`**: Base class for all optimization passes
- **`rtl_opt_pass`** (line 126): Specialization for RTL-level passes that inherit from `opt_pass`
- **`pass_data`** (line 40): Metadata structure containing pass type, name, properties, and timing info

### **Pass_Expand: GIMPLE to RTL** (`gcc/cfgexpand.cc:7010`)
- Converts GIMPLE intermediate representation to RTL form
- Handles basic blocks, control flow, and statement expansion
- First major step in the RTL pass pipeline

### **Representative RTL Optimization Pass: Pass_Combine** (`gcc/combine.cc:15268`)
- Performs instruction combining to reduce RTL instruction sequences
- Exemplifies typical RTL pass structure with `gate()` and `execute()` methods
- Demonstrates how RTL passes inherit from `rtl_opt_pass`

### **Register Allocation Pass: Pass_IRA** (`gcc/ira.cc:6205`)
- Integrated Register Allocator for assigning hardware registers
- Critical for code quality and register pressure optimization

### **Final Code Generation: Pass_Final** (`gcc/final.cc:4340`)
- Generates target architecture assembly code
- Calls `rest_of_handle_final()` for prologue/epilogue and instruction emission
- Final step that produces executable machine code

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete details including files, symbols, execution chain, and a detailed narrative explaining the entire RTL pass organization and flow.

\"GCC's RTL (Register Transfer Language) passes are organized through a class hierarchy defined in gcc/tree-pass.h. The base class is opt_pass, from which rtl_opt_pass extends as a specialization for RTL-level transformations. Each pass has associated metadata in a pass_data structure that defines the pass type, name, properties, and timing information.\\n\\nThe RTL pass chain begins with pass_expand (gcc/cfgexpand.cc:7010), which implements the critical gimple-to-RTL conversion. This pass uses IRA (Integrated Register Allocator) to assign hardware registers to virtual registers and optimize register pressure throughout the function.\\n\\nThe final code generation pass is pass_final (gcc/final.cc:4340), which generates the final assembly output. It outputs the target architecture's assembly instructions through the ASM output file.\\n\\nThe RTL pass chain is orchestrated through passes.def (gcc/passes.def), which uses NEXT_PASS macros to define the order of execution. Key passes execute in sequence: after pass_expand generates RTL, optimization passes like pass_combine improve the RTL, register allocation passes like pass_ira assign registers, and finally pass_final generates the target assembly code. \"GCC's RTL (Register Transfer Language) passes are organized through a class hierarchy defined in gcc/tree-pass.h. The base class is opt_pass, from which rtl_opt_pass extends as a specialization for RTL-level transformations. Each pass has associated metadata in a pass_data structure that defines the pass type, name, properties, and timing information.\\n\\nThe RTL pass chain begins with pass_expand (gcc/cfgexpand.cc:7010), which implements the critical gimple-to-RTL conversion. The pass_expand class inherits from rtl_opt_pass and implements the execute() method that performs the initial expansion from GIMPLE intermediate representation to RTL form, handling basic blocks, control flow, and statement expansion.\\n\\nA representative RTL optimization pass is pass_combine (gcc/combine.cc:15268), which performs instruction combining to reduce RTL instruction sequences. It demonstrates the typical structure of RTL passes: inheriting from rtl_opt_pass, implementing a gate() method for optimization control, and an execute() method that calls rest_of_handle_combine() to perform the actual optimization work.\\n\\nAnother important RTL optimization pass is pass_ira (gcc/ira.cc:6205), which performs integrated register allocation and movement optimization. This pass uses IRA (Integrated Register Allocator) to assign hardware registers to virtual registers and optimize register pressure throughout the function.\\n\\nThe final code generation pass is pass_final (gcc/final.cc:4340), which generates the final assembly output. This pass calls rest_of_handle_final() which orchestrates the final processing steps: assembling function prologue, emitting RTL instructions as assembly, handling exception tables, and assembling the function epilogue. It outputs the target architecture's assembly instructions through the ASM output file.\\n\\nThe RTL pass chain is orchestrated through passes.def (gcc/passes.def), which uses NEXT_PASS macros to define the order of execution. Key passes execute in sequence: after pass_expand generates RTL, optimization passes like pass_combine improve the RTL, register allocation passes like pass_ira assign registers, and finally pass_final generates the target assembly code. This pipeline transforms high-level GIMPLE code through increasingly low-level representations until producing executable machine code.\"\n}\n",
